Having completed this book on the end, which is a concluding work in science according to your description and comes after Al-Zahrawi's comprehensive treatise with its own complementary part that you have referred me to, I am instructed herein as much so that together we can delve into surgery through hands.
Since surgery with the hand is established in our region and since it has been for a long time known everywhere within us alone (if you understand this Latin phrase as referring to knowledge or practice that was once common but now only exists in certain texts): until perhaps science of his work perishes, there will be an end sought; those who searched after him are left without other remains than the skimpy descriptions found here and among ancient books whose hands have worn away. It has happened due to errors they encountered on their way before reaching definitive intentions in such writings: Visa est mihi (here it is my wish), that I fulfill this work together with you according to its own time of use, expressions, abbreviations, and also through the addition made by declaration, as well as concerning all tools used for surgery. Thus having read these instructions within a book on cauterization equipment and other instruments related to operation: once again it is necessary that I complete this work in accordance with intention (meaning intended use), expression (specific terms or descriptions), abbreviation (shortened forms of words) as stated, and also according to the additional information provided within declarations.
Because it is not found a good surgeon who possesses his work with hands in this time of ours: for the art of medicine is long and requires an author to practice beforehand (indicating knowledge) science of Anatomy, as narrated by Galenus, until he understands how members are joined together or separated from one another; also their shapes, forms, joint connections between them in union with others: along with the cognition that each bone has regarding its own skeleton (which includes all types of bones and teeth), arrangement within themselves on which they rest upon each other. Therefore he must understand as well how blood arises from veins flowing into vessels to leave their exit points, in addition also what quietens heartbeat or causes pain at a certain location with the help of hot springs: not forgetting that it is necessary for him firstly know about organs and bodily exits; he must understand all this well beforehand if one wants success.
And because Hippocrates said that a name with many words and little work is especially suited to the art of surgery.
Now we have told about this subject at the beginning of this book.
For who is not skilled in anatomy and knows what we have told about it so that he will no longer fall into error because men are destroyed by them: I myself saw many of these people make up their minds without this science or knowledge from which they proceed, having neither the skill nor experimentation.
What happened was that I saw a foolish surgeon who infected his patient with scrofulous swellings and made some cuts into the woman' startling blood vessels: as a result, her blood flowed until she died in the hands of this maniac.
And I saw another doctor who was presumed to extract the stone from an ageing patient's body: which had become quite large itself as it grew bigger and older over time (a phenomenon Albucasis himself commented on). Unfortunately this maniac surgeon did not know how or when he should stop working, nor could I determine if there would be any benefit to such a treatment. On the topic of lacerations and their treatment through cautery: Albucasis believed that discussions on the quality of surgical instruments like iron tongs used for cauterization are excessively verbose but subtle in knowledge, reflecting a deeply scientific understanding while remaining secretive or occult to others.
1. Even though Albucasis had spoken on this subject among many wise individuals, they disagreed with him and I find that the discussions are insufficient for me due to my fear of overextension in conversation about these surgical instruments and techniques used by cauterization.
1. I argue that cauterization provides a universal benefit to all kinds of wounds without considering the material composition: except for two types - one being heat-related injuries absent external application (calida) and another dry injury also independent of direct stimuli or materials involved (sicca). These exceptions showcase Albucasis' understanding that cauterization, while beneficial in most cases, requires specific considerations when dealing with unique wound types.
1. In the case of other injuries where heat and dryness are present together but also involve material (like foreign bodies or debris), differing opinions arose among Albuc 1. Some indeed said that cautery is suitable for those injuries as well. This implies a broader acceptance of the use of heat and iron or other conductive materials to manage wounds beyond just lacerations, suggesting alternative applications may have been recognized by 1. Others argued the opposite view that cautery is not suitable for such ailments as well; specifically citing heat and dryness (caliditate ac siccitate). Since fire inherently represents heat (ignis est caliditas), it would be inappropriate to use something hot or even cold, which can also cause further harm when the injury is already from warmth or arid conditions. This position indicates a nuanced understanding of wound treatment that considers not just external temperatures but their effects on healing processes and potential for additional damage before cauterization might be considered at all by Albucasis or his contemporaries.
And he who speaks against him said that by means of Cauterium it is performed incision or burning for every hot and dry illness that occurs within the human body; because when you compare a living man's body with its moisture, as if likened to fire, then inevitably you find his body cold.
And indeed I say by his words: because at some point now it has left me through experiment.
However it should not come to pass unless he has already been tried and exercised in the chapter of Cauterii operation itself; having known for a long time the diversity of human complexions, as well as the disposition towards diseases within themselves and their causes and accidents, along with the spaces they occupy temporally.
However there is no fear of these remaining persons for the use [of Cauterium]: especially with regard to diseases that are cold and moist. Now all the physicians have nourished themselves with this [discourse on cauterization]: and they did not disagree therein.
And he knows that his son understands [the secret of curing through Cauterium with fire and its virtue over burning medicines]: for it is simple, whose action does not reach the body unless cauterized: nor does a member join in union with another except to nerve parasitic growth.
The action of medicine with burning has come to this [that it extends from the body's members]: and perhaps even happens within the member itself; making difficult healing possible, or causing death.
Fire because of its subtlety and goodness does not do that [cauterize] unless it is in excess.
Now indeed it becomes clear to us through the experience of trial and study with art [surgery], as well as being stationed over urging things along in reality; hencefors, because of this he has been released from that long narrative.
And if it were not so that this book of mine is closed to you, we would reveal to your secretly hidden mysteries in fire and the nature of such operations as they expel diseases through language philosophically demonstrated with intent to cure minds afflicted by ailments.
And the son knows that they disagree at the time when it was fitting to do a hot iron and choose better timing with words.
And I say that the hot iron was meant for all time: therefore, because a harmful effect occurs due to being engulfed by water, it is drawn into injury along with the treatment itself. Particularly if the hot iron is due to acute pain from indispenerable needs such as wounds that do not endure delay: henceforth it happens because of fear born out of this, which concerns a greater harm than any minor injury caused by tardiness in time.
And it will not fall to the mind of such a son who does not fear unless they are influenced by foolish or inept physicians: for these individuals believe that diseases treated with hot iron do not return forever; and so they endorse this misconception, which is incorrect because there would be no use of fire except within medicine's practice. Specifically to treat conditions like complexion alterations and loss of moisture due to causes such as fever or chills that result in pain: for these individuals wrongly conclude a cure by themselves without the aid of medical treatment which requires this hot application, because there would be no need for fire unless it served within medicine.
Nevertheless, the hot iron is superfluous to medicine through excessive or unjustified surgery and operation efforts: as well as arrogance towards one's own domain; it is possible that healing will return a patient for some time period according to their condition regarding complexion and location of illness, provided they are not suffering from an ailment requiring the administration of hot iron. This happens because preparation occurs within them: which succeeds in returning directly back into themselves through food intake and similar provisions (not if there is disease), as part of its inherent curative action that does not necessitate external fire application, since it returns without this need for medicinal practices outside the body.
The delicate pain under the excessively moist and swollen limb is due to humidity, like that of dental burning therapy, which makes it possible for him not to return with pain there. But this hurts little.
But really that speech is just talking nonsense again: because they say it's about the last medicine in surgery (cutorium), which does not lead to this thing intended therein by themselves, nor with any other aftercare associated therapy as well; since those who use such believe it provides a cure when it has been given no curative treatment and nothing else is done afterwards.
But on the contrary of this opinion is true, and intent in that medicine which they claim as last surgery: it's not so unless when we administered to any patient with disease for some curative means (medical methods), then gave those medical treatments; afterward apply our own cauterism proper methodology therapy. After applying this procedure, the reason of saying that such medicine is last in surgery no longer exists: because as it was originally intended by them themselves and multistolidorum physicians - whom they think to be ignorant fools with many opinions about health matters- does not refer to those actual practices which we have administered beforehand, but instead follows misguided words of the unlearned.
But the ancients said that caustic with gold is better than caustic with iron; and did not say this except because of equality in metal (gold's value), sublimity of substance, and also it does not make a place where pus may arise. But this is not absolutely true; for I have already tried that out and found it to be false: because itself does not make a cause without other things (without additional medical interventions) on some bodies only, but rather exacerbates the condition by introducing heat where dryness should suffice.
And indeed that is a good and better caustic than iron, as they said: because it does not burn like fire but rather cools the area with less discomfort to patient's flesh while still promoting healing of wounds through its cauterizing effect However, when you take an iron cauterium from fire into gold and do not declare it to be so before using it on the subject according to the amount of poison produced by its heat because of blackening with oil; and after proper treatment for coldness has been applied as well as placing a layer above this incision, when these treatments are complete, then melts in fire and is poured into layers.
Therefore, because the instrument falls from that into its employment; and since our cautery with iron is more nearly to nature in this respect: it approaches nearer accordingly towards surgical operations.
And I indeed have arranged this chapter on cautery according to the sections from head to foot, in order that one seeking it may find what is desired about such a matter herein mentioned.

Chapter One.
Know this sickness which often happens to boys at birth; when the midwife tightens around the boy's head without cutting it off.
And also happen for a cause that is not known.
And I myself have not heard this sickness in others besides children; and of those whom it touched with death, to which reason therefore do I say that these things should be stopped by me from operating on them.
And I myself saw a boy whose head was full of water and which grew magnificently every day until it could not bear the weight on its own head; as well as that wetness increased up to his death: for this reason do I say that these things should be stopped by me from operating them.
And whether the wetness is between skin and bone or underneath the skull above the brain matter itself: for this reason do I say that these things should be stopped by me from operating them.
And if there is a wetness between skin and bone and also the skull cap above brain matter itself (and it is an abscess), then at that time one must find in the middle of the cranium's fissure, which lies nearly north to south: as for its length, let it be about two knots long until wetness flows. In this way do I say these things should not undergo operation.
And that is the form of a splinter wound.

Now I have said the treatment of wounds that suits books and will say here their healing by hand and with medicine according to its support..
I say therefore that wounds are of many kinds according to where they fall and what causes them..
Therefore where they fall often the wounds are as when struck with a stone or cut by knife edge; and incisions like cutting open fishes' bellies for their guts to be removed, also percussing of them upon lancea, ligno, sagittae et similibus.
Wounds which fall according to where the body falls are as a wound on head if it hits above crown of skull; also falling upon neck (collum) or breast-bone (pectus); shoulder, chest and abdomen: there with like members in case..
And I am a teller of certain wound treatments putting forth this reasoning and rule for the remaining wounds..

On restoring an anchor.
Chapter Eleven.
Uncommonly do bones of anchors break. But if they break, then the bones are not fractured except for a comminution at their extremities; and they split along length, and fall away towards the interior parts of them: it happens that there is pain in that place with an entry point or puncture wound, and numbness falls upon that which has broken.
And in fact the restoration is to spread your hand over it until you have bound up its broken form as appears there.
That if the bone is broken only at its extremities, then such a break will be made to correspond with one's natural figure as prepared by equation until it becomes similar in shape.
If the bone is broken lengthwise or inclines towards the inside: then I must make an intervention on its extremity and continue until such repair of that person' endured their fracture has been prepared for restoration. When then you have made it equal, put an overlay on that very thing itself and afterwards place a splint over the same from wood or skin: but attach firmly without allowing any shifting of either pieces nor removal of said splints during healing until your repair has been sufficiently prepared for recovery.
